  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>I've noticed IndexWriter's ctor commits a first commit (empty one) if a fresh Directory is passed, w/ OpenMode.CREATE or CREATE_OR_APPEND. This seems unnecessarily, and kind of brings back an autoCommit mode, in a strange way ... why do we need that commit? Do we really expect people to open an IndexReader on an empty Directory which they just passed to an IW w/ create=true? If they want, they can simply call commit() right away on the IW they created.</p> 
                  <p>I ran into this when writing a test which committed N times, then compared the number of commits (via IndexReader.listCommits) and was surprised to see N+1 commits.</p> 
                  <p>Tried to change doCommit to false in IW ctor, but it got IndexFileDeleter jumping on me .. so the change might not be that simple. But I think it's manageable, so I'll try to attack it (and IFD specifically !) back <img class="emoticon" src="/jira/images/icons/emoticons/smile.png" height="16" width="16" align="absmiddle" alt="" border="0">.</p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

So I\'m reluctant to remove that check ... thought I still think we should differentiate between a newly created index on a fresh Directory, to a stale NFS problem. Maybe we can pass a boolean isNew or something like that to the ctor, and if it\'s a new index and the last commit point is missing, IFD will not throw the exception, but silently ignore that? So the code would become something like this:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003e    \u003cspan class=\\\"code-keyword\\\"\u003eif\u003c\\/span\u003e (currentCommitPoint == \u003cspan class=\\\"code-keyword\\\"\u003enull\u003c\\/span\u003e &amp;&amp; href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/LUCENE-2386?focusedCommentId=12855726&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12855726\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"shaie\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Shai Erera\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12855726_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'11\\/Apr\\/10 14:24\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-04-11T14:24:43+0000\'\u003e11\\/Apr\\/10 14:24\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eAs I indicated in an email, Solr tests failed (sorry for not running them before). After some investigation (thanks Robert !), that\'s the problem: before this change, IW always committed first on an empty directory. It called SegmentInfos.commit(dir), which by a chain of calls ensured the directory exists (in FSDir) by calling file.mkdirs().\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAfter this change, that chain of calls did not happen ... yet somehow tests we still passing for Lucene. Some investigation shows that the Solr tests that failed used SingleInstanceLockFactory, or NoLockFactory. By default, FSDir uses either SimpleFSLF or NativeFSLF. The IW.ctor calls LF.makeLock and obtain, which for these two LFs meant that calling file.mkdirs ... and thus the problem was hidden. SingleInstanceLF and NoLF don\'t do that !\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSo first, a test which uses FSDir and one of these LFs need to be created, so we catch that problem in Lucene code (this is not related to Solr &#8211; just a missing test in Lucene). Second we need to fix IW ctor, or Dir or whatever.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI\'ve added that code to IW.ctor, as a sanity check to make sure it works - and indeed all Solr tests pass. So that\'s one option, even though a bit messy.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"code-keyword\\\"\u003etry\u003c\\/span\u003e {\\n  directory.createOutput(\u003cspan class=\\\"code-quote\\\"\u003e\\\"temp\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e).close();\\n} \u003cspan class=\\\"code-keyword\\\"\u003efinally\u003c\\/span\u003e {\\n  directory.deleteFile(\u003cspan class=\\\"code-quote\\\"\u003e\\\"temp\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e);\\n}\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAnother option is to add to Directory a prepareForWrite() or simply prepare() which will be called by IW. A default empty impl on Directory, and file.mkdirs on FSDirectory should be enough.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eA third option is to define clear semantics for dir.listAll(), to throw a NoSuchDirectoryException and then change IndexFileDeleter to ignore that exception if OpenMode of IW is CREATE*. It kind of makes sense - if the directory is empty, why bother looking for any index files. Lucene code today already expects that exception to be thrown in SegmentInfos.getCurrentSegmentGeneration &#8211; so we kind of say \'either you use RAMDirectory, or a sub-class of FSDirectory, and then that\'s what we expect\'. So it\'s not so much of a backwards change ...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eWhile dir.prepare() or prepareForWrite() is very explicit ... it\'s not protective enough - one can still call listAll w\\/o calling prepareForWrite (why would you call it if you just want to list files) so I\'m not sure which is the best option ... Maybe the last option is the best as at least the caller should not assume anything about the state of the directory. Just prepare to handle the NoSuchDirectoryException, vs. \'there is a directory but it\'s empty\' case.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI\'ll revert my commit until this is resolved.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"shaie\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12855726_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=shaie\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"shaie\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Shai Erera\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12855726_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'11\\/Apr\\/10 14:24\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-04-11T14:24:43+0000\'\u003e11\\/Apr\\/10 14:24\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    As I indicated in an email, Solr tests failed (sorry for not running them before). After some investigation (thanks Robert !), that\'s the problem: before this change, IW always committed first on an empty directory. It called SegmentInfos.commit(dir), which by a chain of calls ensured the directory exists (in FSDir) by calling file.mkdirs(). \\n\\n After this change, that chain of calls did not happen ... yet somehow tests we still passing for Lucene. Some investigation shows that the Solr tests that failed used SingleInstanceLockFactory, or NoLockFactory. By default, FSDir uses either SimpleFSLF or NativeFSLF. The IW.ctor calls LF.makeLock and obtain, which for these two LFs meant that calling file.mkdirs ... and thus the problem was hidden. SingleInstanceLF and NoLF don\'t do that ! \\n\\n So first, a test which uses FSDir and one of these LFs need to be created, so we catch that problem in Lucene code (this is not related to Solr &#8211; just a missing test in Lucene). Second we need to fix IW ctor, or Dir or whatever. \\n\\n I\'ve added that code to IW.ctor, as a sanity check to make sure it works - and indeed all Solr tests pass. So that\'s one option, even though a bit messy. \\n  \\n  try  {\\n  directory.createOutput( \\\"temp\\\" ).close();\\n}  finally  {\\n  directory.deleteFile( \\\"temp\\\" );\\n}\\n \\n  \\n\\n Another option is to add to Directory a prepareForWrite() or simply prepare() which will be called by IW. A default empty impl on Directory, and file.mkdirs on FSDirectory should be enough. \\n\\n A third option is to define clear semantics for dir.listAll(), to throw a NoSuchDirectoryException and then change IndexFileDeleter to ignore that exception if OpenMode of IW is CREATE*. It kind of makes sense - if the directory is empty, why bother looking for any index files. Lucene code today already expects that exception to be thrown in SegmentInfos.getCurrentSegmentGeneration &#8211; so we kind of say \'either you use RAMDirectory, or a sub-class of FSDirectory, and then that\'s what we expect\'. So it\'s not so much of a backwards change ... \\n\\n While dir.prepare() or prepareForWrite() is very explicit ... it\'s not protective enough - one can still call listAll w\\/o calling prepareForWrite (why would you call it if you just want to list files) so I\'m not sure which is the best option ... Maybe the last option is the best as at least the caller should not assume anything about the state of the directory. Just prepare to handle the NoSuchDirectoryException, vs. \'there is a directory but it\'s empty\' case. \\n\\n I\'ll revert my commit until this is resolved.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-12855727\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/LUCENE-2386?focusedCommentId=12855727&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12855727\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"shaie\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12855727_verbose\\\" \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12855747_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'11\\/Apr\\/10 16:33\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-04-11T16:33:22+0000\'\u003e11\\/Apr\\/10 16:33\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Actually I consider this a bug in IW\'s ACID transactional semantics... \\n\\n The \\\"I\\\" in ACID is \\\"isolation\\\", meaning, a reader shouldn\'t ever see \\nuncommitted changes from a writer. \\n\\n This bug breaks \\\"isolation\\\", ie, if you open with CREATE, today, IW \\nmay or may not slip in a commit on you, depending (rather \\nunexpectedly, and likely the opposite of what you\'d guess) on whether \\na prior index is already there. \\n\\n So IW sometimes will break ACID transactions, and sometimes not, if \\nyou use CREATE. \\n\\n Further, IW really shouldn\'t ever write a commit \\\"automatically\\\" &#8211; it \\nused to do this (with autoCommit=true), but we stopped doing so \\n(except for this bug), now that autoCommit is false. \\n\\n With this fix, IW will never sneak in a commit.  Your app fully \\ncontrols when the transaction (including CREATE, which in Lucene, \\nunlike most RDMBSs, is part of the transaction) becomes visible. \\n\\n  Thats not a very strong argument for a back compat break on a minor release though...  \\n\\n Hmmm... I think the back compat break is very minor.  Also, IW\'s \\nnow-gone autoCommit never \\\"promised\\\" when commits would be made, so \\nthis was really undocumented behavior. \\n\\n Solr\'s test failures were not due to this break; they we actually due \\nto a sneaky bug that otherwise (had we not had Solr\'s tests) would \\nlikely have remained undiscovered for quite some time. \\n\\n And, much of the \\\"noise\\\" in the patch is from tests relying on exact \\nfile names, commit counts, etc.  Plus some of the usual Shai-cleanups   \\n\\n I guess if we really care to, we can emulate the \\\"not quite ACID\\\" bug \\nwhen Version &lt;= 3.1? \\n\\n  The question is also, what happens if you call IndexWriter.getReader() without the initial commit? added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12855870_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'12\\/Apr\\/10 07:19\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-04-12T07:19:46+0000\'\u003e12\\/Apr\\/10 07:19\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eI\'m not sure if we\'re arguing about the same thing here ... why when I open an IW on empty Directory I need an empty segment that\'s created, and from now on never changed, populated or even read? That just seems wrong to me ... when I fixed the tests to not rely on the buggy behavior, I noticed several which count the list of commits (especially the IDP ones) w\\/ a documentation like \\\"1 for opening + N for committing\\\" ...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIt just looks weird that when you open IW a commit happens, a set of empty files are created, but from now on they are never modified, until IDP kicks in, after the second commit ... it\'s nothing like initing the Directory to be able to receive input ..\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAnd I don\'t know what\'s the benefit of doing \\\"new IW()\\\" following by \\\"IR.open()\\\" ... that IR will always see 0 documents, until you call reopen (if commit happened in between). So what\'s the convenience here? that your code can call IR.open once, and from that point forward just \'reopen()\'? That seems low advantage to me, really. Maybe what we should do is fix IR.open to return a null IR in case the directory hasn\'t been populated w\\/ anything yet. Then you can check easily if you should call open() (==null) or reopen (otherwise). Or create a blank stub of IR which emulates an empty Dir, and when reopen is called works well (if the Directory is not empty now) ...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eBTW, FWIW, Solr\'s code did not break from this change at all ... it was the combination of FSDir and NoLF\\/SingleInstanceLF that broke some tests that used it ... I don\'t know how many apps out there are using that combination, but I\'d bet it\'s small? I use that combination, however in my case an IR is opened only after a commit signal\\/event is raised (so I don\'t check isCurrent often or attempt to reopen()). What I\'m trying to say is that this combination is dangerous, and the application needs to ensure that only one IW is open at any given time, and I\'m sure such apps are more sophisticated then opening IW and then IR just for the convenience of it.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"shaie\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12855870_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=shaie\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"shaie\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Shai Erera\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12855870_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'12\\/Apr\\/10 07:19\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-04-12T07:19:46+0000\'\u003e12\\/Apr\\/10 07:19\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I\'m not sure if we\'re arguing about the same thing here ... why when I open an IW on empty Directory I need an empty segment that\'s created, and from now on never changed, populated or even read? That just seems wrong to me ... when I fixed the tests to not rely on the buggy behavior, I noticed several which count the list of commits (especially the IDP ones) w\\/ a documentation like \\\"1 for opening + N for committing\\\" ... \\n\\n It just looks weird that when you open IW a commit happens, a set of empty files are created, but from now on they are never modified, until IDP kicks in, after the second commit ... it\'s nothing like initing the Directory to be able to receive input .. \\n\\n And I don\'t know what\'s the benefit of doing \\\"new IW()\\\" following by \\\"IR.open()\\\" ... that IR will always see 0 documents, until you call reopen (if commit happened in between). So what\'s the convenience here? that your code can call IR.open once, and from that point forward just \'reopen()\'? That seems low advantage to me, really. Maybe what we should do is fix IR.open to return a null IR in case the directory hasn\'t been populated w\\/ anything yet. Then you can check easily if you should call open() (==null) or reopen (otherwise). Or create a blank stub of IR which emulates an empty Dir, and when reopen is called works well (if the Directory is not empty now) ... \\n\\n BTW, FWIW, Solr\'s code did not break from this change at all ... it was the combination of FSDir and NoLF\\/SingleInstanceLF that broke some tests that used it ... I don\'t know how many apps out there are using that combination, but I\'d bet it\'s small? I use that combination, however in my case an IR is opened only after a commit signal\\/event is raised (so I don\'t check isCurrent often or attempt to reopen()). What I\'m trying to say is that this combination is dangerous, and the application needs to ensure that only one IW is open at any given time, and I\'m sure such apps are more sophisticated then opening IW and then IR just for the convenience of it.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small Go, create some SVN repository - it has initial #0 commit inside. I bet all version control systems and all databases have the concept of null initial commit.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nThis empty commit is what discerns empty existing directory from empty lucene index. If you create some docs, index them, then delete and commit, you\'re going to get just the same picture - a directory with a single segments* file (only generation number will differ).\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAnd references to \\\"but from now on they are never modified\\\" are just weird - it\'s a Lucene index dammit, no files are ever modified here.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eBut, what looks \u003cb\u003ereally\u003c\\/b\u003e weird to me is suggestions like\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003eThen you can check easily if you should call open() (==null) or reopen (otherwise). My app, for example, opens an IR and does scheduled reopens. The time interval is small, a reopen over unmodified index is a noop, so this is all beautifully simple and just as effective as waiting for a commit event (like I did in the past, just like you). It opens an IndexWriter with CREATE_OR_APPEND mode before opening the first reader, and is thus guaranteed to have a good index directory regardless of the situation.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nImmediate fix I see is to check whether the directory is empty and do a first empty commit myself - UGLY.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"earwin\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12855889_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=earwin\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"earwin\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Earwin Burrfoot\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12855889_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'12\\/Apr\\/10 08:55\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-04-12T08:55:16+0000\'\u003e12\\/Apr\\/10 08:55\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Meh, that all is just a matter of perspective. \\n\\n It doesn\'t look weird for me that an empty commit happens. \\nIf he doesn\'t need this functionality, he uses another mode, that simple. \\n\\n  But if the app called new IW, add docs and crashed in the middle, the Directory will still remain empty ... which is sort of what, IMO, should happen.  \\n Why so?   \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/LUCENE-2386?focusedCommentId=12855924&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12855924\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"shaie\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12855924_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=shaie\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"shaie\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Shai Erera\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12855924_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'12\\/Apr\\/10 11:26\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-04-12T11:26:25+0000\'\u003e12\\/Apr\\/10 11:26\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eI don\'t think that people need to write that \\\"emptiness-detection-then-commit\\\" code ... if they care, they can simply immediately call commit() after they open IW.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003eIsn\'t opening IW with CREATE* mode called \\\"specifically asking for\\\"?\u003c\\/p\u003e\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIt depends on how you interpret the mode ... for example, you cannot pass OpenMode.APPEND for an empty Directory, because IW throws an exception. The modes are just meant to tell IW how to behave:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eAPPEND - I know there is an index in the Directory, and I\'d like to append to it.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eCREATE - I don\'t care if there is an index in the Directory &#8211; create a new one, zeroing out all segments.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eCREATE_OR_APPEND - If there is an index, open it, otherwise create a new one.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSo if you pass CREATE on an already populated index, IW doesn\'t do the implicit commit, until you call commit() yourself. But if you pass CREATE on an empty index, IW suddenly calls commit()? That\'s just an inconsistency that\'s meant to allow you to open an IR immediately after \\\"new IW()\\\" call, irregardless of what was there? And if you open that IR, then if the index was populated you see the previous set of documents, but if it wasn\'t you see nothing, even though you meant to say \\\"override what\'s there\\\"?\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI\'ve checked what FileOutputStream does, using the following code:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003eFile file = \u003cspan class=\\\"code-keyword\\\"\u003enew\u003c\\/span\u003e File(\u003cspan class=\\\"code-quote\\\"\u003e\\\"d:\\/temp\\/tmpfile\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e);\\nFileOutputStream fos = \u003cspan class=\\\"code-keyword\\\"\u003enew\u003c\\/span\u003e FileOutputStream(file);\\nfos.write(3);\\nfos.close();\\n\\t  \\nfos = \u003cspan class=\\\"code-keyword\\\"\u003enew\u003c\\/span\u003e FileOutputStream(file);\\nFileInputStream fis = \u003cspan class=\\\"code-keyword\\\"\u003enew\u003c\\/span\u003e FileInputStream(file);\\n\u003cspan class=\\\"code-object\\\"\u003eSystem\u003c\\/span\u003e.out.println(fis.read());\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eSecond line creates an empty file immediately, not waiting for close() or flush() &#8211; which resembles the behavior that you\'re suggesting we should take w\\/ IW (which is the \'today\'s behavior\')\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eForth line closes the file, flushing and writing the content.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eFifth line \u003cb\u003erecreates\u003c\\/b\u003e the file, empty, again, w\\/o calling close. So it zeros out the file content immediately, even before you wrote a single piece of byte to it.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eSixth+Seventh line proves it by attempting to read from the file, and the output printed is -1.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI\'ve wrapped the FOS w\\/ a BufferedOS and the behavior is still the same. So I\'m trying to show is that we don\'t fully adhere to the CREATE mode, and rightfully if you ask me - we shouldn\'t zero out the segments until the application called commit(). But we choose to adhere differently to the CREATE* mode if the index is already populated. That\'s an inconsistent behavior, at least in my perspective. It\'s also harder to explain and document, e.g. \\\"you should call commit() if you used CREATE, in case you want to zero out everything immediately, and the Directory is not empty, but you don\'t need to call commit() if the directory was empty, Lucene will do it for you.\\\" &#8211; so now how will the app know if it should call commit()? It will need to write a sort of \\\"emptiness-detection-then-commit\\\"?\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI am willing to consider the following semantics:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eAPPEND - assumes an index exists and open it.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eCREATE - zeros out everything that\'s in the directory \u003cb\u003eimmediately\u003c\\/b\u003e, and also prepares an empty directory.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eCREATE_OR_APPEND - either loads an existing index, or is able to work on the empty directory. No implicit commit is happening by IW if the index does not exist.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eBut I think CREATE is too dangerous, and so I prefer to stick w\\/ the proposed change to the patch so far &#8211; if you open an index in CREATE*, you should call commit before you can read it. That will adhere to the semantics of what the application wanted, whether it meant to zero out an existing Directory, or create a new one from scratch.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"shaie\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12855924_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=shaie\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"shaie\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Shai Erera\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12855924_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'12\\/Apr\\/10 11:26\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-04-12T11:26:25+0000\'\u003e12\\/Apr\\/10 11:26\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I don\'t think that people need to write that \\\"emptiness-detection-then-commit\\\" code ... if they care, they can simply immediately call commit() after they open IW. \\n\\n  Isn\'t opening IW with CREATE* mode called \\\"specifically asking for\\\"?  \\n\\n It depends on how you interpret the mode ... for example, you cannot pass OpenMode.APPEND for an empty Directory, because IW throws an exception. The modes are just meant to tell IW how to behave: \\n \\n\\t APPEND - I know there is an index in the Directory, and I\'d like to append to it. \\n\\t CREATE - I don\'t care if there is an index in the Directory &#8211; create a new one, zeroing out all segments. \\n\\t CREATE_OR_APPEND - If there is an index, open it, otherwise create a new one. \\n \\n\\n\\n So if you pass CREATE on an already populated index, IW doesn\'t do the implicit commit, until you call commit() yourself. But if you pass CREATE on an empty index, IW suddenly calls commit()? That\'s just an inconsistency that\'s meant to allow you to open an IR immediately after \\\"new IW()\\\" call, irregardless of what was there? And if you open that IR, then if the index was populated you see the previous set of documents, but if it wasn\'t you see nothing, even though you meant to say \\\"override what\'s there\\\"? \\n\\n I\'ve checked what FileOutputStream does, using the following code: \\n  \\n File file =  new  File( \\\"d:\\/temp\\/tmpfile\\\" );\\nFileOutputStream fos =  new  FileOutputStream(file);\\nfos.write(3);\\nfos.close();\\n\\t  \\nfos =  new  FileOutputStream(file);\\nFileInputStream fis =  new  FileInputStream(file);\\n System .out.println(fis.read());\\n \\n  \\n\\n \\n\\t Second line creates an empty file immediately, not waiting for close() or flush() &#8211; which resembles the behavior that you\'re suggesting we should take w\\/ IW (which is the \'today\'s behavior\') \\n\\t Forth line closes the file, flushing and writing the content. \\n\\t Fifth line  recreates  the file, empty, again, w\\/o calling close. So it zeros out the file content immediately, even before you wrote a single piece of byte to it. \\n\\t Sixth+Seventh line proves it by attempting to read from the file, and the output printed is -1. \\n \\n\\n\\n I\'ve wrapped the FOS w\\/ a BufferedOS and the behavior is still the same. So I\'m trying to show is that we don\'t fully adhere to the CREATE mode, and rightfully if you ask me - we shouldn\'t zero out the segments until the application called commit(). But we choose to adhere differently to the CREATE* mode if the index is already populated. That\'s an inconsistent behavior, at least in my perspective. It\'s also harder to explain and document, e.g. \\\"you should call commit() if you used CREATE, in case you want to zero out everything immediately, and the Directory is not empty, but you don\'t need to call commit() if the directory was empty, Lucene will do it for you.\\\" &#8211; so now how will the app know if it should call commit()? It will need to write a sort of \\\"emptiness-detection-then-commit\\\"? \\n\\n I am willing to consider the following semantics: \\n \\n\\t APPEND - assumes an index exists and open it. \\n\\t CREATE - zeros out everything that\'s in the directory  immediately , and also prepares an empty directory. \\n\\t CREATE_OR_APPEND - either loads an existing index, or is able to work on the empty directory. No implicit commit is happening by IW if the index does not exist. \\n \\n\\n\\n But I think CREATE is too dangerous, and so I prefer to stick w\\/ the proposed change to the patch so far &#8211; if you open an index in CREATE*, you should call commit before you can read it. That will adhere to the semantics of what the application wanted, whether it meant to zero out an existing Directory, or create a new one from scratch.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12855961_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'12\\/Apr\\/10 13:36\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-04-12T13:36:31+0000\'\u003e12\\/Apr\\/10 13:36\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eI\'m surrendering the issue, any outcome doesn\'t warrant the time spent discussing it.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nMy conclusions are:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eI see no profit in this change.
